## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (continuous-time population dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is the time-derivative of population size P, indicating an underlying ordinary differential equation for population growth with possible density dependence and/or time-varying environmental forcing via t. Typical structures encode per-capita growth as a function of P (crowding, Allee effects) and sometimes explicit seasonality in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (constant per-capita growth rate)
- Constant immigration/emigration: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (net inflow/outflow independent of P)
- Per-capita linear density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (births linear in P with crowding losses ~ P^2)
- Logistic (Verhulst) differential form: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (carrying capacity via c1 = 1/K)
- Theta-logistic (generalized density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible approach to carrying capacity)
- Richards-like generalized logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P)**c2 (skewed growth curve via shape exponent)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / (P + c2)) (deceleration proportional to log distance from an upper bound)
- Ricker-type continuous density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * P) (exponential suppression of growth at high density)
- Allee effect (strong Allee threshold): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) (negative growth below P = 1/c1)
- Allee + carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P - 1) (two equilibria: low-density threshold and high-density limit)
- Time-varying per-capita growth (environmental trend): dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (growth rate changes linearly with time)
- Seasonal forcing of growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environment/seasonality)
- Harvesting/removal (proportional): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (density regulation with exploitation/mortality)
- Harvesting/removal (constant yield): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (constant off-take independent of P)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dP_dt is approximately proportional to P, the per-capita growth (dP_dt / P) is roughly constant → use dP_dt = c * P.
- A negative P**2 term (or factor (1 - c*P)) indicates crowding/competition where per-capita growth declines linearly with density.
- Presence of log(c/(P+c)) suggests Gompertz-type regulation where growth slows with the logarithm of distance to an upper bound.
- An extra low-density factor (c*P - 1) indicates an Allee threshold with a stable extinction state and a critical minimum population.
- Exponential suppression exp(-c*P) implies sharply increasing density effects at high P (often fitting overcompensation-like behavior).
- Additive constants (±c) in dP_dt represent net immigration or constant-yield harvest that does not scale with P.
- A coefficient that is a function of t (e.g., c0 + c1*t) indicates nonstationary environment or long-term trend in vital rates.
- Sinusoidal dependence on t in the growth coefficient indicates seasonal forcing; expect periodic oscillations in P or in dP_dt / P.
- Multiple factors in P (e.g., P*(1-cP)*(cP-1)) imply multiple equilibria (thresholds and carrying capacities) and possible bistability.
- If dP_dt changes sign at a particular P value, encode that equilibrium explicitly as a factor (1 - c*P) or (c*P - 1).
